	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Non-Aligned Movement</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Establishment</th><td>1961 in <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia"><img alt="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Flag_of_Yugoslavia_%281946-1992%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Yugoslavia_%281946-1992%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Flag_of_Yugoslavia_%281946-1992%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Yugoslavia_%281946-1992%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Flag_of_Yugoslavia_%281946-1992%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Yugoslavia_%281946-1992%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_People%27s_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal People&#39;s Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> as the Conference of Heads of State or Government of Non-Aligned Countries</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><div style="line-height:11pt"><b>Website</b><br /><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://mnoal.org">mnoal<wbr />.org</a></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Non-Aligned Movement</b> (<b>NAM</b>) is a forum of 120 <a href="/wiki/Developing_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing world">developing world</a> states that are not formally aligned with or against any major <a href="/wiki/Power_bloc" class="mw-redirect" title="Power bloc">power bloc</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, it is the largest grouping of states worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-NAM_members_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NAM_members-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NAM_about_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NAM_about-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Drawing on the principles agreed at the <a href="/wiki/Bandung_Conference" title="Bandung Conference">Bandung Conference</a> in 1955, the NAM was established in 1961 in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> through an initiative of the Indian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Jawaharlal Nehru</a><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and the Yugoslav President <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a>.  This led to the first Conference of Heads of State or Governments of Non-Aligned Countries.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The term <i>non-aligned movement</i> first appears in the fifth conference in 1976, where participating countries are denoted as "members of the movement".
</p><p>The purpose of the organization was enumerated by <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> in his Havana Declaration of 1979 as to ensure "the national independence, sovereignty, territorial integrity and security of non-aligned countries" in their "struggle against <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neo-colonialism" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-colonialism">neo-colonialism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a>, and all forms of foreign aggression, <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">occupation</a>, domination, interference or <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemony</a> as well as against <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great power</a> and bloc politics."<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The countries of the Non-Aligned Movement represent nearly two-thirds of the United Nations' members and contain 55% of the world population. Membership is particularly concentrated in countries considered to be developing or part of the <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">Third World</a>, though the Non-Aligned Movement also has a number of <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed nations</a>.
</p><p>Although many of the Non-Aligned Movement's members were actually quite closely aligned with one or another of the <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpowers</a>, the movement still maintained cohesion throughout the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, even despite several conflicts between members which also threatened the movement. In the years since the Cold War's end, it has focused on developing multilateral ties and connections as well as unity among the developing nations of the world, especially those within the <a href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">Global South</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_and_the_Cold_War">Origins and the Cold War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins and the Cold War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Non-Aligned Movement as an organization was founded on the <a href="/wiki/Brijuni" title="Brijuni">Brijuni</a> islands in Yugoslavia in 1956, and was formalized by signing the Declaration of Brijuni on 19 July 1956. The Declaration was signed by <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>'s president, <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a>, India's first prime minister <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Jawaharlal Nehru</a> and Egypt's second president, <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdel Nasser</a>. One of the quotations within the Declaration is "Peace can not be achieved with separation, but with the aspiration towards collective security in global terms and expansion of freedom, as well as terminating the domination of one country over another". According to <a href="/wiki/Rejaul_Karim_Laskar" title="Rejaul Karim Laskar">Rejaul Karim Laskar</a>, an ideologue of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Congress party</a> which ruled India for most part of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> years, the Non-Aligned Movement arose from the desire of <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Jawaharlal Nehru</a> and other leaders of the newly independent countries of the third world to guard their independence "in face of complex international situation demanding allegiance to either two warring superpowers".<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The Movement advocates a middle course for states in the <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing world</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Western_Bloc" title="Western Bloc">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Blocs</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. The phrase itself was first used to represent the doctrine by Indian diplomat <a href="/wiki/V._K._Krishna_Menon" title="V. K. Krishna Menon">V. K. Krishna Menon</a> in 1953, at the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. Publisher has a history of plagiarizing and inaccuracy, even before Wikipedia, see WP:PUS, User:Sitush/Common#Gyan (January 2017)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>But it soon after became the name to refer to the participants of the <i>Conference of Heads of State or Government of Non-Aligned Countries</i> first held in 1961. The term "non-alignment" was established in 1953 at the United Nations. Nehru used the phrase in a 1954 speech in Colombo, Sri Lanka. In this speech, Zhou Enlai and Nehru described the five pillars to be used as a guide for <a href="/wiki/Sino-Indian_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Sino-Indian relations">Sino-Indian relations</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/Panchsheel" class="mw-redirect" title="Panchsheel">Panchsheel</a></i> (five restraints); these principles would later serve as the basis of the Non-Aligned Movement. The five principles were:
</p>
<ul><li>Mutual respect for each other's territorial integrity and <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a>.</li>
<li>Mutual non-aggression.</li>
<li>Mutual non-interference in domestic affairs.</li>
<li>Equality and mutual benefit.</li>
<li>Peaceful co-existence.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>
<p>A significant milestone in the development of the Non-Aligned Movement was the 1955 <a href="/wiki/Bandung_Conference" title="Bandung Conference">Bandung Conference</a>, a conference of Asian and African states hosted by Indonesian president <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a>, who gave a significant contribution to promote this movement. Bringing together Sukarno, <a href="/wiki/U_Nu" title="U Nu">U Nu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nasser" class="mw-redirect" title="Nasser">Nasser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nehru" class="mw-redirect" title="Nehru">Nehru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Tito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Nkrumah</a> and Menon with the likes of <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh" title="Ho Chi Minh">Ho Chi Minh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">Zhou Enlai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Norodom Sihanouk">Norodom Sihanouk</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/U_Thant" title="U Thant">U Thant</a> and a young <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a>, the conference adopted a "declaration on promotion of world peace and cooperation", which included Zhou Enlai and Nehru's five principles, and a collective pledge to remain neutral in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. Six years after Bandung, an initiative of Yugoslav president <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a> led to the first <i>Conference of Heads of State or Government of Non-Aligned Countries</i>, which was held in September 1961 in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The term <i>non-aligned movement</i> appears first in the fifth conference in 1976, where participating countries are denoted as <i>members of the movement</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belgrade_Conference,_1961.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg/220px-Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg/330px-Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg/440px-Belgrade_Conference%2C_1961.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3336" data-file-height="2483" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belgrade_Conference,_1961.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Belgrade Conference, September 1961 with representatives from <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Afghanistan" title="Kingdom of Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="Union of Burma">Burma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Cambodia_(1953%E2%80%9370)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Cambodia (1953–70)">Cambodia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire" title="Ethiopian Empire">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pahlavi_dynasty" title="Pahlavi dynasty">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Nepal" title="Kingdom of Nepal">Nepal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somali_Republic" title="Somali Republic">Somalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Ceylon" title="Dominion of Ceylon">Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Sudan_(1956%E2%80%9369)" title="History of Sudan (1956–69)">Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Republic" title="United Arab Republic">United Arab Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Federal_People%27s_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal People&#39;s Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>At the Lusaka Conference in September 1970, the member nations added as aims of the movement the peaceful resolution of disputes and the abstention from the big power military alliances and pacts. Another added aim was opposition to stationing of military bases in foreign countries.<sup id="cite_ref-suvedi_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suvedi-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some members were involved in serious conflicts with other members (e.g. India and Pakistan, Iran and Iraq). 
</p>
<h4><span id="Cuba.27s_role"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba's_role">Cuba's role</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cuba&#039;s role">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the 1970s, Cuba made a major effort to assume a leadership role in the world's  nonalignment movement, which represented over 90 Third World nations. Cuban combat troops in Angola greatly impressed fellow non-aligned nations.
</p><p>Cuba also established military advisory missions, and economic and social reform programs. The 1976 world conference of the Nonaligned Movement applauded Cuban internationalism, "which assisted the people of Angola in frustrating the expansionist and colonialist strategy of South Africa's racist regime and its allies." The next nonaligned conference was scheduled for Havana in 1979, to be chaired by <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>, with his becoming the de facto spokesman for the Movement.  The conference in September 1979 marked the zenith of Cuban prestige.  Most, but not all, attendees believed that Cuba was not aligned with the Soviet camp in the Cold War.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>  However in December 1979, the Soviet Union intervened in Afghanistan's civil war. At the time, Afghanistan was also an active member of the Nonaligned Movement. At the United Nations, Nonaligned members voted 56 to 9, with 26 abstaining, to condemn the Soviet Union. Cuba in fact was deeply in debt financially and politically to Moscow, and voted against the resolution. It lost its reputation as nonaligned in the Cold War. Castro, instead of becoming a high profile spokesman for the Movement, remain quiet and inactive, and in 1983 leadership passed to India, which had abstained on the UN vote. Cuba lost its bid to become a member of the United Nations Security Council and its ambitions for a role in global leadership had totally collapsed.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>  More broadly the Movement was deeply split over the <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War" title="Soviet–Afghan War">Soviet–Afghan War</a> in 1979. Although Moscow's allies supported the Soviet intervention, other members of the movement (particularly <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">predominantly Muslim states</a>) condemned it.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Cold_War">Post-Cold War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Post-Cold War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Because the Non-Aligned Movement was formed as an attempt to thaw out the Cold War,<sup id="cite_ref-suvedi_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suvedi-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> it has struggled to find relevance since the Cold War ended. After the <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup of Yugoslavia</a>, a founding member, its membership was <a href="/wiki/Suspension_(punishment)" title="Suspension (punishment)">suspended</a><sup id="cite_ref-suspended_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suspended-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> in 1992 at the regular Ministerial Meeting of the Movement, held in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> during the regular yearly session of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly of the United Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Najam_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Najam-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The successor states of the Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia have expressed little interest in membership, though <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> have observer status. In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> ceased to be members and joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> is the only member of the Movement in Europe. <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> are the most recent entrants, joining in 2011. The applications of Bosnia and Herzegovina and <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a> were rejected in 1995 and 1998, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Najam_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Najam-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, the Non-Aligned Movement has been forced to redefine itself and reinvent its purpose in the current world system. A major question has been whether many of its foundational ideologies, principally national independence, territorial integrity, and the struggle against colonialism and imperialism, can be applied to contemporary issues. The movement has emphasised its principles of multilateralism, equality, and mutual non-aggression in attempting to become a stronger voice for the global South, and an instrument that can be utilised to promote the needs of member nations at the international level and strengthen their political leverage when negotiating with developed nations. In its efforts to advance Southern interests, the movement has stressed the importance of cooperation and unity amongst member states,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> but as in the past, cohesion remains a problem since the size of the organisation and the divergence of agendas and allegiances present the ongoing potential for fragmentation. While agreement on basic principles has been smooth, taking definitive action vis-à-vis particular international issues has been rare, with the movement preferring to assert its criticism or support rather than pass hard-line resolutions.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The movement continues to see a role for itself, as in its view, the world's poorest nations remain exploited and marginalised, no longer by opposing superpowers, but rather in a uni-polar world,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and it is Western hegemony and neo-colonialism that the movement has really re-aligned itself against. It opposes foreign occupation, interference in internal affairs and aggressive unilateral measures, but it has also shifted to focus on the socio-economic challenges facing member states, especially the inequalities manifested by globalization and the implications of neo-liberal policies. The Non-Aligned Movement has identified economic <a href="/wiki/Underdevelopment" title="Underdevelopment">underdevelopment</a>, poverty, and social injustices as growing threats to peace and security.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/16th_Summit_of_the_Non-Aligned_Movement" title="16th Summit of the Non-Aligned Movement">16th NAM summit</a> took place in <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>, Iran, from 26 to 31 August 2012. According to <a href="/wiki/Mehr_News_Agency" title="Mehr News Agency">Mehr News Agency</a>, representatives from over 150 countries were scheduled to attend.<sup id="cite_ref-MehrNews_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MehrNews-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Attendance at the highest level includes 27 presidents, two kings and emirs, seven prime ministers, nine vice presidents, two parliament spokesmen and five special envoys.<sup id="cite_ref-tehrantimes1_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tehrantimes1-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> At the summit, Iran took over from Egypt as Chair of the Non-Aligned Movement for the period 2012 to 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-allafrica_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allafrica-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and latest one held in Venezuela 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019 <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> suspended their participation in the Movement under the presidency of Venezuela, because their governments did not recognize the legitimacy of <a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_Maduro" title="Nicolás Maduro">Nicolás Maduro</a>'s regime.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organizational_structure_and_membership">Organizational structure and membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Organizational structure and membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The movement stems from a desire not to be aligned within a geopolitical/military structure and therefore itself does not have a very strict organizational structure.<sup id="cite_ref-organizational_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-organizational-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Some organizational basics were defined at the 1996 <i>Cartagena Document on Methodology</i><sup id="cite_ref-Methodology_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Methodology-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The Summit Conference of Heads of State or Government of Non-Aligned States is "the highest decision making authority". The chairmanship rotates between countries and changes at every summit of heads of state or government to the country organizing the summit.<sup id="cite_ref-Methodology_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Methodology-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Requirements for membership of the Non-Aligned Movement coincide with the key beliefs of the United Nations. The current requirements are that the candidate country has displayed practices in accordance with the ten "Bandung principles" of 1955:<sup id="cite_ref-Methodology_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Methodology-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Respect for fundamental human rights and for the purposes and principles of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" title="Charter of the United Nations">Charter of the United Nations</a>.</li>
<li>Respect for the sovereignty and territorial integrity of all nations.</li>
<li>Recognition of the movements for national independence.</li>
<li>Recognition of the equality of all races and of the equality of all nations, large and small.</li>
<li>Abstention from intervention or interference in the internal affairs of another country.</li>
<li>Respect for the right of each nation to defend itself singly or collectively, in conformity with the Charter of the United Nations.</li>
<li>Refraining from acts or threats of aggression or the use of force against the territorial integrity or political independence of any country.</li>
<li>Settlement of all international disputes by peaceful means, in conformity with the Charter of the United Nations.</li>
<li>Promotion of mutual interests and co-operation.</li>
<li>Respect for justice and international obligations.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Policies_and_ideology">Policies and ideology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Policies and ideology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Non-Aligned_Movement_(emblem_-_South_Africa_Conference).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/20/Non-Aligned_Movement_%28emblem_-_South_Africa_Conference%29.png/220px-Non-Aligned_Movement_%28emblem_-_South_Africa_Conference%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/20/Non-Aligned_Movement_%28emblem_-_South_Africa_Conference%29.png 1.5x" data-file-width="279" data-file-height="255" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Non-Aligned_Movement_(emblem_-_South_Africa_Conference).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The South Africa Conference NAM logo</div></div></div>
<p>Chairpersons<sup id="cite_ref-auto_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> of the NAM had included such diverse figures as <a href="/wiki/Suharto" title="Suharto">Suharto</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> militaristic<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> anti-communist, and <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a>, a democratic socialist and famous <a href="/wiki/Internal_resistance_to_South_African_apartheid" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal resistance to South African apartheid">anti-apartheid</a> activist. Consisting of many governments with vastly different ideologies, the Non-Aligned Movement is unified by its declared commitment to <a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">world peace</a> and security. At the seventh summit held in New Delhi in March 1983, the movement described itself as "history's biggest peace movement".<sup id="cite_ref-thomas_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomas-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The movement places equal emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Disarmament" title="Disarmament">disarmament</a>. NAM's commitment to peace pre-dates its formal <a href="/wiki/Institutionalisation" title="Institutionalisation">institutionalisation</a> in 1961. The Brioni meeting between heads of governments of India, Egypt and Yugoslavia in 1956 recognized that there exists a vital link between struggle for peace and endeavours for disarmament.<sup id="cite_ref-thomas_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomas-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 1970s and early 1980s, the NAM also sponsored campaigns for restructuring commercial relations between developed and developing nations, namely the <a href="/wiki/New_International_Economic_Order" title="New International Economic Order">New International Economic Order</a> (NIEO), and its cultural offspring, the <a href="/wiki/New_World_Information_and_Communication_Order" title="New World Information and Communication Order">New World Information and Communication Order</a> (NWICO). The latter, on its own, sparked a Non-Aligned initiative on cooperation for communications, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_News_Agencies_Pool" title="Non-Aligned News Agencies Pool">Non-Aligned News Agencies Pool</a>, created in 1975 and later converted into the <a href="/wiki/NAM_News_Network" title="NAM News Network">NAM News Network</a> in 2005.
</p><p>The Non-Aligned Movement espouses policies and practices of cooperation, especially those that are multilateral and provide mutual benefit to all those involved. Many of the members of the Non-Aligned Movement are also members of the United Nations. Both organisations have a stated policy of peaceful cooperation, yet the successes the NAM has had with multilateral agreements tend to be ignored by the larger, western and developed nation dominated UN.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> African concerns about apartheid were linked with Arab-Asian concerns about Palestine<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and multilateral cooperation in these areas has enjoyed moderate success. The Non-Aligned Movement has played a major role in various <a href="/wiki/Ideological" class="mw-redirect" title="Ideological">ideological</a> conflicts throughout its existence, including extreme opposition to apartheid governments and support of guerrilla movements in various locations, including <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a> and South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_activities_and_positions">Current activities and positions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Current activities and positions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2017</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_US_policy">Criticism of US policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Criticism of US policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In recent years the organization has criticized certain aspects of US foreign policy. The <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a> and the <a href="/wiki/War_on_Terrorism" class="mw-redirect" title="War on Terrorism">War on Terrorism</a>, its attempts to stifle <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>'s nuclear plans, and its other actions have been denounced by some members of the Non-Aligned Movement as attempts to run roughshod over the sovereignty of smaller nations; at the most recent summit, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Yong-nam" title="Kim Yong-nam">Kim Yong-nam</a>, the head of North Korea's parliament, stated, "The United States is attempting to deprive other countries of even their legitimate right to peaceful nuclear activities."<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-determination_of_Puerto_Rico">Self-determination of Puerto Rico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Self-determination of Puerto Rico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 1961, the organization has supported the discussion of the case of <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Political status of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico's self-determination</a> before the United Nations. A resolution on the matter was to be proposed on the XV Summit by the <a href="/wiki/Hostosian_National_Independence_Movement" title="Hostosian National Independence Movement">Hostosian National Independence Movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated. (January 2009)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-determination_of_Western_Sahara">Self-determination of Western Sahara</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Self-determination of Western Sahara">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 1973, the group has supported the discussion of the case of <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara_conflict" title="Western Sahara conflict">Western Sahara's self-determination</a> before the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The movement reaffirmed in its last meeting (Sharm El Sheikh 2009) the support to the Self-determination of the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">Sahrawi</a> people by choosing between any valid option, welcomed the direct conversations between the parties, and remembered the responsibility of the United Nations on the Sahrawi issue.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainable_development">Sustainable development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sustainable development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The movement is publicly committed to the tenets of <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a> and the attainment of the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>, but it believes that the international community has not created conditions conducive to development and has infringed upon the right to sovereign development by each member state. Issues such as globalization, the <a href="/wiki/Developing_countries%27_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing countries&#39; debt">debt burden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trade_justice" title="Trade justice">unfair trade practices</a>, the decline in foreign aid, <a href="/wiki/Conditionality" title="Conditionality">donor conditionality</a>, and the lack of democracy in international financial decision-making are cited as factors inhibiting development.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reforms_of_the_UN">Reforms of the UN</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Reforms of the UN">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The movement has been outspoken in its criticism of current UN structures and power dynamics, stating that the organisation has been utilised by powerful states in ways that violate the movement's principles. It has made a number of recommendations that it says would strengthen the representation and power of "non-aligned" states. The proposed <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations" title="Reform of the United Nations">UN reforms</a> are also aimed at improving the transparency and democracy of UN decision-making. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council</a> is the element it considers the most distorted, undemocratic, and in need of reshaping.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South-South_cooperation"><a href="/wiki/South-South_cooperation" class="mw-redirect" title="South-South cooperation">South-South cooperation</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: South-South cooperation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The movement has collaborated with other organisations of the developing world&#160;&#8211;&#32; primarily the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32; forming a number of joint committees and releasing statements and documents representing the shared interests of both groups. This dialogue and cooperation can be taken as an effort to increase the global awareness about the organisation and bolster its political clout.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_diversity_and_human_rights">Cultural diversity and human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Cultural diversity and human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The movement accepts the universality of human rights and social justice, but fiercely resists cultural homogenisation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="reliable source needed for the whole sentence (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In line with its views on sovereignty, the organisation appeals for the protection of cultural diversity, and the tolerance of the religious, socio-cultural, and historical particularities that define human rights in a specific region.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (August 2012)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Working groups, task forces, committees<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li>Committee on Palestine</li>
<li>High-Level Working Group for the Restructuring of the United Nations</li>
<li>Joint Coordinating Committee (chaired by Chairman of G-77 and Chairman of NAM)</li>
<li>Non-Aligned Security Caucus</li>
<li>Standing Ministerial Committee for Economic Cooperation</li>
<li>Task Force on Somalia</li>
<li>Working Group on Disarmament</li>
<li>Working Group on Human Rights</li>
<li>Working Group on Peace-Keeping Operations</li></ul>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Summits">Summits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Summits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</p>

<p>A variety of ministerial meetings are held between the summit meetings. Some are specialist, such as the meeting on "Inter-Faith Dialogue and Co-operation for Peace", held in Manila, the Philippines, 16–18 March 2010. There is a general Conference of Foreign Ministers every three years. The most recent were in Bali, Indonesia, 23–27 May 2011 and Algiers, Algeria, 26–29 May 2014.
</p><p>The Non-Aligned Movement celebrated its 50th anniversary in Belgrade on 5–6 September 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chairperson">Chairperson</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Chairperson">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <p>A chairperson is elected at each summit meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The Coordinating Bureau, also based at the UN, is the main instrument for directing the work of the movement's task forces, committees and working groups.
</p>

<h2><span id="Members.2C_observers_and_guests"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Members,_observers_and_guests">Members, observers and guests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Members, observers and guests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_members">Current members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Current members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Non-Aligned_Movement_by_Date_Joined.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Non-Aligned_Movement_by_Date_Joined.svg/220px-Non-Aligned_Movement_by_Date_Joined.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Non-Aligned_Movement_by_Date_Joined.svg/330px-Non-Aligned_Movement_by_Date_Joined.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Non-Aligned_Movement_by_Date_Joined.svg/440px-Non-Aligned_Movement_by_Date_Joined.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1314" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Non-Aligned_Movement_by_Date_Joined.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Non-Aligned Movement Member Countries by Year Joined</div></div></div>
<p>The following countries are members of the NAM, arranged by continent, showing their year of admission:<sup id="cite_ref-NAM_members_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NAM_members-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cahoon_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cahoon-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Currently every African country (except <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">Western Sahara</a>) is a member of the Non-Aligned Movement.
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Observers">Observers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Observers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guests">Guests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Non-Aligned_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Guests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is no permanent guest status,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> but often several non-member countries are represented as guests at conferences. In addition, a large number of organisations, both from within the <a href="/wiki/UN_system" class="mw-redirect" title="UN system">UN system</a> and from outside, are always invited as guests.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In a joint letter to the <a href="/wiki/UN_Secretary-General" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Secretary-General">UN Secretary-General</a> sent just prior to unification, the Ministers of Foreign affairs of North and South Yemen stated that "All treaties and agreements concluded between either the Yemen Arab Republic or the People's Democratic Republic of Yemen and other States and international organizations in accordance with international law which are in force on 22 May 1990 will remain in effect, and international relations existing on 22 May 1990 between the People's Democratic Republic of Yemen and the Yemen Arab Republic and other States will continue."<cite class="citation book">Bühler, Konrad (2001). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Ty7NAG1Jl-8C&amp;dq=State+Succession+and+Membership+in+International+Organizations&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s"><i>State Succession and Membership in International Organizations</i></a>. Martinus Nijhoff Publisher.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=State+Succession+and+Membership+in+International+Organizations&amp;rft.pub=Martinus+Nijhoff+Publisher&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft.aulast=B%C3%BChler&amp;rft.aufirst=Konrad&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DTy7NAG1Jl-8C%26dq%3DState%2BSuccession%2Band%2BMembership%2Bin%2BInternational%2BOrganizations%26source%3Dgbs_navlinks_s&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANon-Aligned+Movement" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg/23px-Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg/35px-Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg/45px-Flag_of_North_Yemen.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Yemen_Arab_Republic" title="Yemen Arab Republic">North Yemen</a> is one of the founders in 1961.  <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg/45px-Flag_of_South_Yemen.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Republic_of_Yemen" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Democratic Republic of Yemen">South Yemen</a> joined in 1970. In 1990 both were <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_unification" title="Yemeni unification">unified</a> into a single state which accepted responsibility for all treaties of its predecessors.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> </span>
